Local News

This Port's Yesterday's Hurricane, Rainstorm, and High Tide

Roads Flooded, Ships Suspended

Since the hurricane first arrived the night before last, the roaring wind had subsided, and the intense heat had eased, much to the relief of the city's residents. Yesterday morning, however, thick clouds gathered, and the hurricane continued to blow, though without rain. By noon, sudden showers came, and the sound of wind and rain grew increasingly intense. In the Huangpu River, a high tide surged. By evening, all the roads had flooded, creating a very serious situation. The details are as follows:

Yesterday Evening's Observatory Warning

At 9:00 PM last night, the Xujiahui Observatory issued a special warning, stating that the hurricane had clearly struck the coast near the Zhoushan Islands and was passing through Hangzhou Bay, continuing northwest. Shanghai would experience extremely strong winds and heavy rain, coming from the northeast to the southeast, with the hurricane moving towards the western part of Shanghai.

City Scene Desolate

Amidst the heavy wind and rain, the scene on the city's roads changed dramatically. Low-lying areas were flooded ankle-deep, some even a foot deep. The bitter wind and dreary rain created a desolate atmosphere. All the shops closed early, and by evening, there were very few pedestrians on the roads. Of the various modes of transportation, only cars could still pass. Trams were brought in early and could not carry passengers. Rickshaws, unable to withstand the strong wind and rain, mostly ceased operating, causing significant difficulties for city traffic.

Lights Extinguished Several Times

The lights in the Nanshi and Zhabei areas were extinguished several times due to power lines being broken by the wind and damaged transformers. Although workers were dispatched for repairs, restoration was difficult in the short term. As a result, many streetlights were out by evening. In the Zhabei area, the lights went off and on about three times from 5:00 PM onwards. In the Nanshi area, such as the Nine Acres area, all the lights were out from 10:00 PM onwards. A considerable number of shop signs and window shutters were blown down by the wind onto the roads. In the French Concession, the lights were also extinguished in the evening.

Strong Winds Blow Down Houses

Several houses were blown down by the strong wind and heavy rain. In Zhabei, the chimney of the Zhengtai Dyeing Factory on Minde Road was blown down around 5:00 PM, and the falling bricks injured the owner of the adjacent tofu shop. In Xinminde Xinli, one house was blown down. Around 3:30 PM, near Baker Road and Chengdu Road, several houses were also blown down. There were also several cases of fires caused by broken power lines.

High Tide in the Huangpu River

From 3:00 PM, the wind gradually increased, followed by heavy rain. The tide in the Huangpu River suddenly rose by about two feet. Ferries and sampans all stopped and sought shelter. The white waves were terrifying. It was reported that a barge was wrecked near the Bund Copper Statue Wharf. Many trees on the Bund were broken and felled by the wind. By 11:00 PM, the water level along the Bund had reached waist-deep due to the influx of river water.

A Glimpse of Road Flooding

Roads in lower-lying areas were completely flooded, becoming a "country of lakes" as there was no way to drain the excess water. In the International Settlement, Fuzhou Road, Henan Road, Race Course, Chengdu Road, Carter Road, and in the French Concession, Route SayZoong and low-lying areas of Nanshi and Zhabei were flooded ankle-deep. Pedestrians had to lift their skirts and hold up their clothes to walk. Many motorcycles broke down on the road and were unable to move forward.

Drowning in Water Leads to Electrocution

Fu Baiqing, who lived at No. 262 Fuzhou Road, was playing in the water in front of his neighbor's house at No. 278 during the heavy wind and rain last night. Unaware that a broken power line was lying in the water, Fu accidentally stepped on it and was immediately electrocuted to the ground, unconscious. He was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment by the Lao Zha public concession police car, but it was too late. He died and was sent to the mortuary for an autopsy.

Overview of Roads This Morning

Due to the gradual rise of the tide in the Huangpu River, our reporter traveled by car to various locations at 1:00 AM this morning to conduct on-site investigations. The wind and rain made driving difficult. Abandoned cars were everywhere. The tide in the Huangpu River was rising westward. When the reporter was writing this report, the tide had already spread to Stone Road and was threatening to reach the Race Course. The Suzhou Creek also overflowed its banks. The ships anchored in the river to take shelter from the wind were densely packed, with their hulls as high as the houses on the shore. Nanjing Road, which is usually paved with wood, absorbed water and expanded, causing it to bulge upwards. Countless pieces of wood floated on the surface. The road surface was damaged in many places. When the wind stops and the water recedes in the future, the losses will be immeasurable. The Sixteen Puli and Gaochang Temple areas of Nanshi were completely flooded. All the lights were out, and the car traveled through a world of darkness. Even the police officers on duty had temporarily taken shelter. The walls of the residence of Dr. Ding Yuqin, a female doctor on Xunchidao Street, near the Great East Gate, collapsed, exposing the beds, tables, and furnishings inside. Many of the advertising billboards erected by the Public Works Department on various roads were blown down by the wind.

House Collapses This Morning, Injuring People

Around 1:00 AM this morning, the house of Wang Yongxing Laundry at No. 191 Henan Road, near Baoshan Road, collapsed in the strong wind. Four people inside the house were crushed to death because they were unable to escape in time. Three others were seriously injured. They were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment by a fire engine. Their condition is quite dangerous.

Foreign Ships Sheltering from the Wind

This hurricane was even more severe than the last one. Yesterday afternoon, as the wind approached Shanghai and there were showers, foreign ships, which usually do not delay their schedules, had to anchor and stop en route. The Pacific Mail Steamer President Madison, of the Great Lai Yang Company, which came to Shanghai from Hong Kong via Luzon Island and was due to arrive in Shanghai yesterday morning, encountered the hurricane at Sanjiaoshui. For safety, the ship's owner had it anchored at sea. The Japanese Mail Company's San Francisco mail ship Ryuta Maru also sent a telegram to Shanghai yesterday, saying that it had sailed to Hirado Island to take shelter from the wind and would postpone its arrival in Shanghai. The Sino-American cargo ships Coolbaugh, and Kersaint, etc., were originally scheduled to enter the port today, but are now sheltering from the wind in the Yellow Sea and cannot sail here.

Sino-Japanese Liner Service Suspended

The Sino-Japanese liners scheduled to depart yesterday included the Nippon Yusen Kaisha's Shanghai Maru to Yokohama, the Rokko Maru to Osaka-Kobe, the Mikasa Maru, which goes to Kobe first and then to New York, and the Seimo Maru, among others, totaling six or seven ships. The cargo was fully loaded and the passengers boarded, but due to the continuing hurricane and the huge waves in the Yellow Sea, which made navigation very difficult, the ships did not dare to venture out and announced a postponement of their departure.

Coastal Vessels All Stopped

Having learned from the previous accidents involving the Weisheng, Guang Sheng, and Yichang, all coastal vessels refrained from sailing. The Swire Southern Ocean liner Suiyang remained in Wusong. The Northern Ocean ship Shuntian, the Niuzhuang ship Chongqing, and the Jardine Southern Ocean ship Zesheng, the Nisshin's Shanghai Maru, Huashan Maru, etc., all remained in Shanghai. The Xinjiang and Chongqing, which were already prepared for departure, sailed to Yangshupu, but due to the excessive wind, they all anchored and waited.

Yangtze River Vessels Remain Suspended

The strong wind has gradually approached Shanghai and reached the Hangzhou Bay area. There is also a hurricane in the Yangtze River Estuary. Therefore, all Yangtze River vessels did not depart on the 24th. Yesterday, the six companies' Yangtze River vessels that should have left Shanghai, including the Wuhu, Nanyang Maru, and Gonghe, had their cargo loaded, but because the wind was even stronger than the previous day, they were ordered to stay in Shanghai and not depart, waiting for the wind to stop tomorrow before traveling upstream with the previous day's Yangtze River vessels. As a result, mail to various ports along the Yangtze River was also indirectly delayed.

Large Numbers of Ships Anchored at the Mouth of the Song River

Yesterday afternoon, only the British Mail Company's mail ship Camora, loaded with silk and tea worth 2.5 million yuan and a large number of passengers bound for Europe, risked sailing because mail ships cannot be delayed. However, after arriving in Wusong, it immediately anchored and waited for the wind to stop before proceeding. In addition, the Jardine's Jinsheng, Guisheng, the EWO's Glen Line, and the China Merchants' Anning and Taiping also sailed to the mouth of the Wusong River and anchored nearby. In total, more than twenty import and export ships were blocked at the mouth of the Song River. Only a few import ships arrived yesterday, including the Yangtze River vessels Jiangda, Xiangtan, Shashi, Pinghe, and the Great Lai's Cleveland, and the Taikoo's Jinan. The rest were unable to sail into the Huangpu River.

Observatory Denies Shanghai Will Have Major Flooding

Social Affairs Bureau Sends Personnel to Inquire, Father Zi Firmly Declares

Father Zi of the Xujiahui Observatory issued a special denial in response to a Nanjing telegram published in a newspaper yesterday, claiming that according to the observatory's predictions, Shanghai would experience a ten-foot-high tidal wave around September 12th (Lunar August 1st). He stated that the observatory had never made such a prediction and did not know what the telegram was based on. He expressed regret that attributing such an alarming message to the observatory had frightened the citizens.

Upon seeing a Nanjing telegram in a local newspaper yesterday reporting that Shanghai would experience major flooding, stating that according to a report from the Shanghai Observatory, a flood of twelve feet was expected to occur in Shanghai on the first day of the eighth lunar month, the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau found this news to be quite strange. How could it be known that such a major flood would suddenly occur on the first day of the eighth lunar month, and how was this twelve-foot measurement calculated? Since it was claimed to be a report from the Shanghai Observatory, the Bureau immediately sent personnel to the Xujiahui Observatory to investigate. M. BURGAUR, the acting director of the observatory, firmly stated that there was no such report and that he did not know where the so-called Flood Relief Association obtained this information. The director will issue a letter of confirmation, which will state, in brief: "Currently, personnel from the Social Affairs Bureau have brought the News and the Shen Bao, which contain a news article stating that a major flood will occur in Shanghai on the first day of the eighth lunar month (lunar calendar). After investigation: (1) This observatory has never issued this news; (2) This news must be the result of personal speculation, causing considerable disturbance to society, which this observatory is quite concerned about." The observatory also requested that the Social Affairs Bureau investigate the source of the news and the location of the Flood Relief Association.

Note: This newspaper does not have this record, and we are deeply shocked to be involved. We hereby make a solemn statement.

Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces Yesterday

Relief Authorities Have Concrete Plans

Enthusiastic Individuals Continue to Actively Raise Funds

The responsible authorities issued a statement yesterday regarding the urgent relief efforts for the floods in various provinces, stating that they have concrete plans. Enthusiastic individuals from both China and abroad are also working hard to raise relief funds. The details are as follows:

Song Ziwen Discusses Disaster Relief Policies

Yesterday, Chairman Song of the Disaster Relief Committee issued the following statement: "In order to decide on the steps for disaster relief, we must first understand the various issues involved in disaster relief work. The first step should be to prepare food, shelter, and medicine for the tens of thousands of homeless victims. The second step, after the water recedes, is to prepare food for those who cannot work and to employ the victims to repair old dikes and build new dikes, providing relief through labor. During this period, we will also widely encourage farmers to rush to plant vegetables and wheat before winter arrives. Finally, we should prepare to provide farmers with seeds and agricultural tools for spring plowing. According to our committee's observations, this work cannot be completed in a matter of weeks and will likely take at least six months. The committee will need to concentrate the government's allocated funds, private donations, and various food supplies as much as possible to provide relief. Currently, the government will need to bear 60 million yuan for urgent relief work. In addition to preparing funds to purchase ordinary supplies, we plan to purchase 50 million yuan worth of grain on credit. In summary, the losses of fields, crops, and property in this flood are so great that even 100 million yuan in cash may not be enough to meet the urgent needs of tens of millions of victims. In addition to the government's various forms of assistance, we also have the full support of Chinese and foreign individuals, charitable organizations, religious groups, the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, the Huai River Conservancy Commission, the Whangpoo Conservancy Board, and other official public works agencies. Furthermore, missionaries in the interior who are familiar with local conditions can also assist with the current relief efforts and future projects. In view of the above situation, the committee firmly believes that the relief work can be handled exclusively by this committee, but we hope that all private charitable organizations can cooperate with this committee. To reduce expenses and strictly control the budget, all income and expenditure of funds will be carefully reviewed by the members of the accounting and auditing groups to prevent fraud. The names of the members are listed below: Bennett (Citibank), Chen Guangfu (Shanghai Bank), Hubbard (Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation), Lawrence (Reiss & Co.), Ji Fusun (Zhejiang Industrial Bank), Lin Kanghou (Shanghai Banking Association), Lu Bohong (Nanshi Electric Light Company), Omura (Mitsui & Co.), Song Hanzhang (Bank of China), Waldson (Accounting Advisor, Ministry of Finance), Zhang Jia'ao (Bank of China) (Director of this group)."

News from the Relief Committee

Donation Collection Agencies

The Disaster Relief Committee announced today that in addition to eleven foreign banks and twenty-five domestic banks, the Yida Tongchun, Fukang, Fuyuan, Zhixiang, and five other native banks have also agreed to collect donations.

The Situation of Disaster Victims in Wuhan

According to reports from Committee Member Li Zushen, the Disaster Relief Committee has established more than seventy shelters in the Wuhan area, which can accommodate 200,000 refugees. He also stated that there are 10 million disaster victims in Hubei Province, 5 million of whom are in urgent need of relief. The actual number of disaster victims in the Wuhan area is estimated to be 400,000.

Zhu Cha and Others Postpone Flight to Hankou

Zhu Qinglan, a standing committee member of the relief committee, and Bai Liangzhao, a member of the North China Charity Federation, were dispatched by the National Government's Disaster Relief Committee to investigate the details of the floods in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. They were scheduled to fly to Hankou from Shanghai at 7:00 AM yesterday to investigate the disaster situation along the way. However, due to the heavy wind and rain in Shanghai yesterday, the plane could not take off. Zhu and others waited for the plane at Longhua Airport for about an hour, but as a result of the bad weather, the flight was postponed until today or tomorrow, depending on when the wind and rain subside.

Foreign Representatives Hold Disaster Relief Meeting

The North China Daily News reported that representatives of the foreign community in Shanghai preparing for disaster relief held another meeting at the Fook Company yesterday (24th) afternoon, chaired by Major Nathan. They elected members of the executive, finance, and fundraising groups and resolved to organize one or two hospital ships with the funds raised to go to Hankou to treat diseases and prevent epidemics. According to the chairman's report, he has already contacted a ship, and the monthly rent is 10,000 yuan, plus medicine and other expenses, estimated to cost about 60,000 yuan in total for three months. Currently, only 12,000 yuan has been raised, and efforts must be made to raise more funds.

Unbearable Disaster in Xinghua

The flooding in Jiangbei this year is particularly severe, with Xinghua being the worst affected. A visitor from Jiangbei recently spoke about the tragic situation in the county, which is unbearable to hear. The county's terrain is low-lying, more than three feet below the bottom of Hongze Lake, shaped like a pot. Water must fill the entire area before it can seep into neighboring counties. This time, the three dams were opened simultaneously, pouring straight down. The west is about two feet higher than the east. The western and southern villages around Jiuli Jiaowazhuang were the first to be hit, and many houses were washed away and lives were lost due to the suddenness of the disaster. Almost none of the farmers who were in the fields harvesting the young rice survived. The three dam openings totaled more than 180 feet. Traditionally, a dam could only be opened every four days, with the water level rising four inches, and it had to be announced three days before opening the dam to allow the downstream people to prepare. This year, the river workers were unaware of the situation and opened the three dams suddenly within three days (the South Gate Dam was secretly opened by the river workers), and the water rushed down like an arrow, scouring the banks and causing destruction overnight. The ground in each village suddenly deepened by several feet. Farmers fled for their lives, fathers, sons, wives, and children unable to take care of each other. Some climbed onto rooftops or clung to trees, their cries were unbearable to hear. In the eastern part of the county, there are still one or two embankments that have not been breached. On the ninth of this month, news of a collapse was heard. Those guarding the embankment were unable to escape and dozens of people were washed away with the water. The fields and crops in the embankment were immediately submerged. The residents in the embankment were forced to live in the open on the embankment, suffering from hunger and heat. Many died, the old and weak groaned, and the young and strong moved away. There has been no relief to this day. Currently, except for a few high spots that have not been flooded, the lowest point in the county is five feet deep. Outside the city, there is a vast expanse of water. Where treetops are visible above the water, that is where the villages and markets used to be. The flooding of the entire county is terrible, and the water level is still rising every day, and the future consequences are unknown. The county has suffered from continuous famine for four years and was already in a precarious situation. Now that it has suffered this unprecedented disaster, the people are bound to starve to death. The provincial government has only allocated 5,000 yuan for urgent relief, which is a drop in the bucket and does not help. We hope that the great philanthropists in Shanghai will take into account the severity of the disaster in the county and allocate relief funds in abundance, so that the people of the county will be grateful beyond measure.

Recent News from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association

Continued Reports from Various Counties (7) Liuhe County: This county experienced continuous heavy rain this summer, with mountain floods and rising river tides, resulting in the collapse of embankments on the southwest and east sides, inundating 99% of the fields. People and livestock were washed away, and houses were destroyed, creating a heart-wrenching scene. It is estimated that more than 400,000 acres of fields were affected, exceeding half of the county's total acreage. Nearly 100,000 disaster victims were displaced, gathering on small hills and high ground, their cries echoing in the air. (8) Liyang County: This county, also known as the ancient Jingjiang area, has extremely low-lying terrain. This summer, with continuous rain and mountain floods, most of the polders were breached. The crops in the higher fields were exposed to the floodwaters. The middle farmers exhausted their resources to save the embankments in the hope of having a harvest. However, in mid-July, there was another heavy rain, and the water level rose further. As a result, all the polders in the area were submerged. From Yixing in the east to Jintan in the north, and from the northwest to Hekouzhen, there was no embankment that was not breached and no crop to be seen. In addition, the water from the mountains in southern Anhui and the floodwaters from Wuhu, Gaochun, and the Yangtze River poured down, destroying and washing away people, livestock, houses, farmland, and crops. Looking from a high point, thousands of square miles were flooded, and the villages and residents were locked in by water, with no way to escape, and were left to die. (9) Suqian County: Since summer, the county has experienced continuous rain, which has inundated the crops. On the 2nd of this month, there was another heavy rain, causing the Yi and Yun rivers to rise sharply. The areas where the embankments collapsed have all become swamps, especially the Yaowan and Huanghe areas. (10) Huaiyin County: The county is located at the intersection of the Yun and Huang rivers and borders Hongze Lake to the southwest. Since the summer, there has been continuous rain, and the Huai and Yun rivers have risen, causing a severe disaster. In the first, second, sixth, and seventh districts, the water depth is about eight feet, and the shallowest is three to five feet. Houses and autumn crops have been destroyed and submerged. Hundreds of thousands of victims are living in the open, their faces showing signs of malnutrition. (11) Jintan County: The county's industry and commerce have never been developed, and the livelihoods of the common people depend entirely on agriculture. However, on July 5th of this year, there was a torrential rain that lasted all night, and the low-lying areas all became swamps. The embankments were also submerged in the water. Farmers ran around, shouting and rescuing, exhausting their mental and physical strength, hoping to make up for a fraction of the loss. However, on July 23rd and 24th, there was another downpour, and the streets were flooded, cutting off traffic. The suburbs were an ocean, and animals and houses were washed away.

Wu Zhaozeng's Letter to Wang Yiting and Di Chuqing

Regarding the Issue of Opening the Sanmao You River

Respectful greetings to Mr. Yiting and Mr. Chuqing,

I recently received your instructions stating that the citizens of Xinghua County have sent a telegram stating that the county has become a swamp because the Dafeng Yuhua embankment is blocking the water from flowing into the sea, causing great suffering to the people. They requested that the company be telegraphed to quickly open the Sanmao You River to facilitate drainage. You also expressed your willingness to sacrifice the Dafeng Company to save the people. Your bodhisattva-like heart is admirable and worthy of our respect. Regarding this matter, ten days ago, when the Cheluo Dam was opened, I received a letter from Leng Yujun Yuqiu, which had already telegraphed Dafeng to quickly discuss with Yuhua opening the Mao You East Dam as a temporary route for the western water. Later, I received a clever telegram from the company, stating that the water level in Dongtai was rising two or three inches every day, and that it was still two feet lower than the highest point of the people's houses. It has been more than ten days since the Cheluo Dam was opened. The company is located to the east of Dongtai, which is higher than the hinterland. How can it block the water from flowing into the sea? This is a fact. The rumors are turbulent, which is understandable given the urgency of the situation. However, what will be the consequences of provoking ill feelings? Scholars and officials are ignorant of the situation in the lower reaches of the river, and are occasionally deceived. The provincial government also lacks accurate surveys and announcements to maintain a fair discussion. I cannot help but worry. Now, I would like to briefly tell you two gentlemen about the situation in the lower reaches of the river, which has been recorded in history, and the current state of the salt fields: (1) Regarding the entry of diverted water from the east into the sea, during the Qianlong period, Tang Bin listened to the words of local scholars and officials and submitted a memorial. At that time, Jin Fu was the river governor, and strongly stated that the sea embankment could not discharge the water from the lower reaches of the river, and that a heavy dike should be built to block the water from entering the sea from Qingkou. The matter was submitted to the ministers for discussion and reply. Yu Chenglong advocated opening the sea embankment. As a result, scholars, officials, and court officials jointly criticized Jin Fu, who was almost punished and even had his fat subordinate Chen Hanzhi removed from his post to appease public opinion. Later, Yu Chenglong and Sun Zaifeng were specially sent to open the lower reaches of the river directly to the east into the sea. Over the years, due to the actual situation, the sea embankment could not be opened in the end. Yu Chenglong admitted his mistake, and Jin Fu's original proposal was adopted. Jin Fu believed that the water discharged by the canal should be centered on the lower reaches of the river, which included several counties, with a length of more than 300 miles from north to south and more than 200 miles from east to west, shaped like a pot. Only by digging in the bottom of the pot could the depth of the pot be increased. It would be impossible to go directly east into the sea, and opening it would be useless. Liu Qin's Dingmao poems on sensitive events state: "East of Bangjiang Bank, the accumulated water is always vast, covering seven prefectures and counties, and the coastal area is particularly elevated." This ancient saying proves that the coast is high. Today, Xinghua and Gaoyou have become vast lakes, while Dongtai, Yancheng, and Funing, which are located in the east, are not yet severely affected by water, which also shows that the terrain is different. Now, pointing to the salt reclamation company's embankment as blocking the western water should be proven with reason, and cannot be an act of transferring anger. Previously, I saw Zhuang Songlao's instructions on the Huai River diversion plan, which also stated that the water should be introduced into the river in the south and into the sea in the north, with the Chuanbang River as its tributary. It can be seen that those with practical experience have the same views. Those who can divert the water into the sea have five ports that can be connected. It is impossible to draw water from farmland. (2) The salt reclamation company is located outside the Fan Dike, providing a livelihood for the salt workers who are unable to survive on the coast. Since its establishment, it has dredged the old large ports on the west water side that enter the sea, and has not blocked them. The meridian and river, which has the function of transportation and irrigation, also has its own segment-specific models. It is a pity that it has not been able to get the government's help to connect them. There is also a plan to expand the Mao You River entering the sea, and dozens of plans have been completed, which can be used for temporary discharge. According to Jiangbei's arguments, there is a proposal to make the water run on the ground against the dikes of the salt reclamation companies, in order to restore the ancient floods. If this is the case, then the country should not seek construction in order to achieve the effect of drought and flood prevention. Salt reclamation shareholders have invested for more than ten years, and millions of debts and investments have not been paid. Now, they are still comforting themselves by saying: "Although we have suffered losses, hundreds of thousands of poor and helpless salt workers are gradually making a living." Now, the people in the lower reaches of the river, due to the water damage, have targeted the salt reclamation companies. We have telegraphed the reclamation area to properly arrange for it to comfort the people. Now, I see the reclamation area's telegram reporting that some people are inciting ignorant people to freely excavate, and yesterday I also presented a petition to the provincial government, requesting that it be stopped to avoid riots. The salt reclamation company is not greatly affected by the western water because the terrain is higher, but it is only afraid of the sea tide. If the sea tide is allowed to backflow, it will turn the reclaimable area that has been cultivated for more than ten years into bare teeth, and the water in the lower reaches of the river will still not be able to leave the five ports and enter the sea from the company's boundary, because the land is originally higher than the water in the lower reaches of the river, and the water cannot go uphill. This matter has been investigated by the local pro-people assemblies, and they have said that the people's lives in the interior are important, and the reclamation area's lives are also important. We should aim for mutual benefit. Moreover, the lower reaches of the river are only affected by the western water for one year, while the company's land is affected by the sea tide, and it will take ten years of cultivation to restore it. Although the company has a plan for the Sanmao You River, only the middle Mao You is connected to the sea, while the south Mao You is trapped by the economy and has not yet been dredged, and is still far from the coast. The north Mao You does not even have a river shape. The Dafeng north section has no embankment along the coast, and the western water can still run rampant. The local people know this, but they still spread their words to scare people, so it is suspected that they have an effect. In short, the reason why the western water is a disaster for the lower reaches of the river is actually in the upper reaches, west of the Yun Dike, where the bottom of the lake and the bottom of the river are gradually silting up, and the capacity is becoming shallower. Now, the Huai River diversion is ready to proceed, and the flooding of the canal can be reduced in the future. Chief Sun said that water conservancy is not something that can be done by Jiangsu Province alone, and he is truly aware of the situation. After all, there has never been water conservancy that is divided and governed by boundaries. You two gentlemen have always had clear eyes and no obstacles in your hearts. Therefore, I am not afraid of trivial words and hope that you will consider the actual situation, weigh the importance of things, and uphold justice. Those who are spared are many, and rescuing the disaster is the same merit. Please give your instructions if appropriate.

With respectful greetings,

Wu Zhaozeng

Yangzhou Fellow Villagers Association Telegram to Yangzhou Chamber of Commerce

The Yangzhou Eight Counties Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai yesterday sent the following express telegram to the Yangzhou Chamber of Commerce, et al.: “To Wang Jingting, Dai Xingyi, Hu Xianbo, Ruan Dachong, and all esteemed gentlemen of the Yangzhou Chamber of Commerce: Our hometown has suffered a catastrophic flood, the people are displaced and wailing in despair, a truly miserable sight. We members of this association are deeply concerned about our homeland and upon hearing this news, we immediately convened an emergency meeting. We have publicly appointed Shen Dingchen, Ting Fuchen, Ruan Mubai, and Chen Yangnian to request relief from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association. We also implore your esteemed chamber and gentlemen to provide details of the actual disaster situation in each county, and request photographs to be submitted to the Relief Association to aid in publicity. Fearing that requesting relief will take time and the need is urgent, we will prepare donation registers and distribute them among the association members for fundraising. The collected amount will be remitted immediately. We respectfully submit this telegram for your consideration. Respectfully, the Executive Committee of the Yangzhou Eight Counties Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai.”

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association Undertakes Emergency Relief Efforts

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association reports that Hankou has been submerged for over twenty days, with a foul stench spreading disease and a severe shortage of food and drink. In addition to allocating funds for emergency relief, the association yesterday shipped four thousand bottles of cholera medicine, with director Yan Chengde dispatching personnel to distribute it to curb the spread of disease. They have also prepared five hundred bags of flour and seventy boxes of bread, which will be shipped to Hankou immediately for distribution. It is reported that strong northerly winds are blowing in Hankou, and there are concerns that the river may rise again. The association held an emergency meeting yesterday to discuss effective relief methods. The Sino-Foreign Relief Association has been receiving numerous letters and telegrams from various locations requesting relief, detailing tragic disaster situations. Benevolent individuals from various places are also generously donating to support the relief efforts. (1) The Yongshan Society, recognizing the significant donation of funds and medicinal supplies from overseas Chinese Hu Wenhu, was inspired to send 5,000 yuan. (2) The Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce wired 10,000 yuan. (3) The Chinese in Penang, organized as the "Chinese Relief Association for the Ancestral Country's Disasters," wired 5,053 taels, 3 mace, and 3 fen. (4) The Selangor Grocery Merchants remitted 3,000 yuan, designated for flood relief. (5) Chinese employees of HSBC (through Gong Ziyu's fundraising efforts) donated 1,000 yuan. (6) Shan Xianmo from Zhejiang Shaoxing raised 810 yuan. (7) The Shanghai Public Cemetery Office donated 1,000 yuan, to be distributed among various disaster areas. (8) The Zhejiang Hangzhou Xie De Shantang forwarded 600 yuan from nine households, including Shen Zhuzhai, and others. Countless individuals have also made donations under their own names, demonstrating a commendable eagerness to help. However, given the vastness of the affected area and the severity of the disaster, although donations are considerable, there is still a shortage of funds for distribution. It is hoped that warm-hearted and benevolent individuals will continue to contribute to help these disaster-stricken people. The Sino-Foreign Relief Association acknowledges the widespread concern and generosity of people from all walks of life regarding this year's major floods. To facilitate donations from people in the Nanshi area, they have consulted with the Nanshi branch of the Bank of China to act as a collection point for the association's donations. Benevolent individuals in Nanshi can now make donations conveniently at the branch.

The Ningbo-Shaoxing Emergency Relief Association for the Hankou Disaster received a donation of essential medicines from the Hu Qing Yu Tang pharmacy, including 2,000 packets of Huoxiang Zhengqi Pills, 500 packets of Chunyuang Zhengqi Pills, 2,000 packets of Jisheng Powder, 2,000 packets of Wushi Tea, 1,000 bottles of Wolong Dan, and 500 packets of Shaqi Pills. Regarding cash donations from Ningbo fellow villagers, over 20,000 yuan has been collected in the past two days. The association will collect all types of food and medicine and transport it to Hankou today. It is also reported that the association received telegrams from Li Zushen and Yin Huichang reporting on the disaster situation, excerpts of which are below: "The water has receded yesterday, now at 53.1 feet. People's hearts are gradually calming down. Ningxing Mingfang." "Telegram 1: Along the way, the river water is vast, and the disaster situation on both banks is tragic. The water in Hankou has not yet receded, but the rising trend has slightly stopped, and people's hearts are somewhat calmer. However, some fellow villagers are hesitating due to responsibilities and property concerns. Now, it is planned to advise women and children to leave first. Please be informed. Respectfully."

Various Sectors Cooperate to Assist in Relief

The Commercial Press Translation Institute Employees Donate Salaries for Disaster Relief: The Commercial Press Translation Institute launched a campaign to provide relief for the flood disaster. The proposal was made by the institute's labor union cadres and approved by the group leaders' meeting. The plan stipulates that employees with monthly salaries below 100 yuan donate one day's salary, those with salaries between 100 and 200 yuan donate one and a half days' salary, and those with salaries above 200 yuan donate two days' salary. It is reported that other departments and units within the Commercial Press will follow suit.

Newspaper Delivery Workers Union Collects Funds for Relief: The Shanghai Newspaper Delivery Workers Union plans to collect 1,500 yuan to provide emergency relief. It is reported that 500 yuan will be contributed first today or tomorrow.

Vocational Education Society Employees Donate Salaries to Aid Relief: In light of the severity of the floods in various parts of the country, the employees of the China Vocational Education Society have initiated a campaign to donate salaries to aid relief. Each person will donate voluntarily. In addition to the Zhouji Society already directly sending funds to the Emergency Relief Association, the society's administrative department reports that over 300 yuan has been raised by just over twenty people. The society's workers have also joined, bringing the total amount to over 30% of each person's salary. The funds have already been sent to the Emergency Relief Association for forwarding to the disaster area. Affiliated organizations are also contributing.

Chinese Employees' Association of the Shanghai Municipal Council Aids Flood Relief: In light of the severe floods in various provinces, the Chinese Employees' Association of the Shanghai Municipal Council recently launched a membership donation drive. Donations have been very enthusiastic. The total amount will be handed over to the Flood Relief Association as soon as it is collected.

Shanghai Municipal Union 26th Branch Holds Disaster Relief Meeting: The 26th Branch of the Shanghai Special District Municipal Union held an emergency disaster relief meeting yesterday. Chairman Wang Hanliang presided over the meeting and discussed disaster relief measures. (1) (Omitted). (2) Issue leaflets and clear disaster area illustrations to promote public awareness. (3) Appoint the entire organizing committee as the fundraising committee. (4) Send letters to member merchants and firms, requesting generous donations. The minimum request is to donate 5% of the business income within ten days. Contributions over a longer period are welcomed. (5) If donations are approved, please send them directly to the Disaster Relief Committee. (6) Send letters to member merchants and firms requesting them to place disaster relief boxes or bamboo tubes in front of their stores, marked with "Disaster Relief Donation" so that customers can donate generously. When the boxes or tubes are opened, please send representatives from the Disaster Relief Committee to collect the donations to ensure propriety. The meeting adjourned after discussions.

Youth Propaganda Corps Holds Performance to Raise Relief Funds: The Provisional Disaster Relief Group of the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Corps will hold a flood relief performance at the corps' lecture hall at 8:00 PM on the 29th of this month (Saturday) to actively raise relief funds. All proceeds from ticket sales will be used for flood relief in the disaster areas.

Zhabei Water and Electricity Company Employees Rehearse Kunqu Opera for Relief: The employees of the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, who have been studying Kunqu Opera for years, are raising funds for flood relief. In addition to the directors, supervisors, and all employees making every effort to donate, the employees' association has launched an initiative to hold a Kunqu Opera rehearsal performance at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association on Xizang Road on the evening of September 6th. Record of Yesterday's Inauguration Ceremony of Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

Central Representative Gives Three Points of Instruction, Guest Attendance Reaches Over Four Hundred

The Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Kuomintang's third Executive and Supervisory Committee members were elected from the seventh City Representatives Congress on July 1st, and submitted twice the number of candidates to the central government for approval. They took office on the 17th of this month and held an inauguration ceremony yesterday at 10 AM in the building's auditorium. Zhang Yuejun was appointed by the Central Committee to oversee the swearing-in. Guest attendance was about four hundred. The ceremony was hosted by the Executive Committee Chairman Pan Gongzhan.

Oath-taking order: (1) Music plays to open the meeting. (2) Everyone stands at attention. (3) Sing the party anthem. (4) The central oath-taking member takes their position. (5) Each committee member takes their position. (6) Give the highest respect to the Party National Flag and the portrait of the leader. (7) The chairman respectfully reads the leader's last will. (8) Moment of silence. (9) Chairman's report. (10) Oath-taking. (11) The Central Representative's speech. (12) Guest speeches. (13) Replies. (14) Music plays. (15) Photo. (16) Meeting adjourned.

Yesterday, representatives from various organizations and groups attended the ceremony, including representatives from each organization, group, district party headquarters, and district branch offices, totaling approximately four hundred.

Chairman's Report: After the ceremony, Chairman Pan Gongqing delivered his report, stating, "Central Oath Taker, representatives of various organizations and groups, comrades: Today is the inauguration ceremony for the third Executive Committee and Supervisory Committee members of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang. We are honored to have Committee Member Zhang from the central government here to oversee the oath-taking, and representatives from various organizations and groups to provide guidance. As we hold this inauguration ceremony today, we should review the past work, determine future directions, and clearly understand the responsibilities of our comrades, so as not to fail the expectations of everyone. Now, I will briefly report on the work of comrades in Shanghai in recent years. There are things that are worth comforting ourselves with, but in general, we are still far from our ideals. Shanghai has been very important from the end of the Qing Dynasty until now, from the perspective of the revolution and the standpoint of the party. The cultivation of revolutionary forces and the launch of revolutionary work all started from Shanghai. Especially when the Northern Expeditionary Army conquered the Yangtze River basin and the communist elements became arrogant and subversive, endangering the party and the country, the purge movement started earliest and most thoroughly in Shanghai. Other provinces such as Guangdong, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Hubei suffered the tragedy of being burned, looted, and massacred by red bandits, but Shanghai was fortunate to escape this fate. The reason is that the general comrades and citizens of Shanghai were able to work together under the leadership of the central government. Therefore, this city has neither suffered the extreme labor-capital conflicts that Wuhan once experienced, nor the trampling by red bandits in Guangzhou and Haifeng, and it has not suffered the burning and killing in Jiangxi and Hunan. We can recognize that we can be slightly comforted by this. Moreover, because of the stability of social order in Shanghai, industry and commerce have been able to maintain their foundation and gradually develop and prosper, leaving a piece of intact work for the Central Plains and a fraction of vitality for the country. In recent years, the central government has been able to calmly suppress bandits and suppress rebellion, and make smooth progress militarily, so that the great cause of unification can be completed sooner or later. The assistance of Shanghai is undeniable. Just take this flood as an example. The disaster affected sixteen or seventeen provinces, with five or six thousand people being forced from their homes, with tens of thousands in gold being lost. Other areas are suffering from human-caused disasters and natural disasters. Fortunately, Shanghai, with its social stability and financial resources, has gathered the strength of its comrades to provide aid to our compatriots in other provinces and cities. The stability of Shanghai, seemingly a passive achievement, is something that we and our citizens can be proud of. However, there are many aspects of the work of comrades in Shanghai in recent years that are not satisfactory. The direction of future work should be changed. From the perspective of the spirit of party members, comrades in Shanghai seem to be more lax than in the era of secret work. If this continues, party members will become officials and the party headquarters will be close to the bureaucracy. It is important to know that the work of the party does not necessarily have to be done on a writing desk in the party headquarters. If everyone can do their best, use their own position to publicize doctrines, develop people's hearts, assist in autonomy, and carry out construction, then assuming that there are 6,000 party members in this city, there will be the strength of 6,000 comrades. Otherwise, only the efforts of the staff within the party headquarters will be available, and the city party headquarters, with one hundred people, combined with the district party headquarters and branches, will only have three or four hundred people. The difference is so small, and the error is so big. Is this not equal to reducing its strength? Therefore, starting from this session, the erroneous concept that comrades who do not work in the party headquarters do not have to do the work of the party should be absolutely corrected. Every party member should do his best for the party at all times and work hard. This is the first point. Secondly, the party anthem personally written by the Leader contains the two phrases "Counseling your many scholars, as the people's vanguard." The so-called vanguard is like the army's daredevil team and assault team, unafraid of sacrifice and difficulty, determined to kill oneself to achieve benevolence and abandon life to take righteousness. Only with this spirit can we lead the masses, and the masses will believe in the party members and thus obey the leadership of the party. If the party headquarters is high above and only issues an order or an official document to force execution, the masses may not dare to disobey, but how can it last? The Leader's instruction of 'vanguard of the people' originally wanted us to suffer first before the masses, not to flaunt our power above the masses. If every party member can recognize that the benefits belong to the people and the obligations belong to the party, not only will the masses be convinced, but the party will be the masses. The work of the party and the completion of the revolution will all be accomplished without any doubt. We certainly have the leader of our party, Mr. Sun Yat-sen's doctrines, spirit, morality, and learning, which can influence the people. But every party member must continue the spirit of the Leader and obey the doctrines of the Leader, so that our party can continue to influence the people and be their guide. In this way, the strength will be great and can complete a very difficult revolutionary work. From this session onwards, the executive and supervisory committee members should pay attention to the cultivation of party morality and party friendship, so that every comrade has the responsibility to serve the people and sacrifice for the party. This is the starting point for the development of the party's work in this city. This is the second point. Today, my comrades held an inauguration ceremony, very sincerely and frankly admitting the shortcomings of past work, and taking it as a direction for future efforts to improve. I hope that the central oath-taker and the representatives of various organizations and groups will give more guidance. Finished."

Oath-taking Committee Members: After the Chairman's report, each supervisory committee member, under the supervision of the Central Representative, raised their right hand and read the oath as follows: "I swear with utmost sincerity to abide by the Leader's last will, believe in the Party's doctrines, obey the Party's orders, abide by the Party's program and discipline, complete the national revolution, and realize the Three Principles of the People to seek China's freedom and equality. I will never act selfishly to mislead the Party or harm the organization. If I violate this oath, I am willing to receive the most severe punishment from the Three People's Principles." The names of the committee members who took the oath are as follows: (Executive Committee Members) Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, Tao Baichuan, Chen Xizeng, Yang Qingyuan, Chen Kecheng, Jiang Huaisu, Du Gang, Cai Hongyin. (Alternate Executive Committee Members) Hou Dachun, Lu Jingsheng, Huang Zaoxiong, Zhou Feicheng, Zhu Peng (Absent). (Supervisory Committee Members) Wang Yansong, Tong Xingbai, Huang Xuchu, Deng Tongwei, Xiong Shihui (Absent). (Alternate Supervisory Committee Members) Chen Bai, Zhang Zaibai.

Central Speech: After the oath, the Central Representative Zhang Yuejun gave a speech, stating: "Dear Committee Members, honored guests: Today, the committee members of the City Party Headquarters of this city are holding an inauguration ceremony, and the Central Committee sent brothers to come and oversee the ceremony. When the city held the Seventh City Representatives Congress last time to elect you all, the Central Committee also sent representatives to participate, which was a great honor. Just now, the chairman gave a detailed explanation and strict inspection and reflection on the importance of Shanghai's party affairs, the importance of Shanghai's party affairs and the relationship between the central government and the whole country, and the achievements of Shanghai's party affairs in recent years. We are very satisfied, and there is no need to add more explanation. Recalling when brothers participated in the Seventh City Representatives Congress, they once said that in addition to electing executive and supervisory committee members, the duties of the representatives congress are to accept the work reports of various agencies and examine and judge them as the standard for work, and to examine past work and determine the future direction of party affairs in the city. At that time, the representatives from the city gathered and studied with great concentration and proposed many important motions and decided on many concrete programs, resulting in a very satisfactory outcome. The resolutions of each case are deeply valuable and practical. Those who implement these resolutions are the committee members who are taking office today. I hope that the committee members will follow the guidance of the central government and implement the resolutions of the congress to make progress in the party affairs of this city. Brothers dare to believe that as long as you all work together with one heart, you will surely achieve your goals, because most of the committee members of this session are re-elected, and a few new committee members are also the comrades who are most familiar with the party affairs of this city. Naturally, you can achieve twice the result with half the effort. This is the first point I want to contribute to you all. The slogan 'Loyal Comrades Unite' was seen at the last City Representatives Congress and at today's inauguration ceremony. At the same time, brothers have been running around in various places in recent years and have often found such slogans. To be honest, brothers have felt infinitely emotional. On the surface, it is a very ordinary slogan, but why is it necessary to call on loyal comrades to unite? Of course, it is because there are some who are not loyal or because some who are loyal are unable to unite and unable to cooperate. The strength of the party is based on spiritual unity and unified will. Only with a spirit of unity and a unified will can there be mutual love and sincerity. Only then can the strength of the party be manifested and the revolutionary work can be completed. Not only in our country but in all the famous parties in the world, the organization, actions, and thoughts of their party members are simply completely militarized and disciplined. There is absolutely no individual will, only the will of the party. There is absolutely no individual action, only the action of the party. There is no such thing as loyalty and disloyalty in a party. All comrades have feelings, and I hope you will think deeply about this, and people must strive to achieve no longer seeing this kind of slogan and hearing this kind of shout, then the party morality and party friendship of our party will surely improve, and the strength of the party will be enough to eradicate all reaction and guarantee the peace and unification of the country. This is the second point I want to contribute to you all. The importance of the Fourth National Congress of the Communist Party of China is to contribute the items for discussion issued by the central government for a detailed and careful study for presentation to the Central Government in order to facilitate discussion."

Committee members' reply: After the speeches by the guests, Tong Xingbai, the representative of the executive and supervisory committee members, gave a reply, which has been omitted.

Local News Two

Detectives Arbitrarily Investigate Pedestrian Disputes

Neither Having a License Nor Acting Under Orders to Inspect

The plaintiff says more than ten silver dollars have been confiscated

Yesterday around four o'clock in the morning, a man named Chen Yuqing was returning from a business meeting with a friend near the North Railway Station when six or seven men suddenly approached him and stopped him. They searched him arbitrarily and found nothing. As a result, they took away more than ten silver dollars that were in his pocket. At first, Chen suspected they were plainclothes military police acting under orders to inspect pedestrians. But when he saw them snatching his silver dollars, he suspected that they were not good people. He asked them to show their badges, but they had no evidence of any official capacity. Chen immediately called the police to arrest them. One of them, surnamed Huang, claimed to be a detective from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's detective team, who had been ordered by his captain to inspect pedestrians. The police officer asked to see Huang's detective license, but Huang claimed that he had left his gun license at home and had not brought it out. The police officer, seeing no evidence, detained both Chen and Huang at the Fourth District Headquarters. The district chief conducted a preliminary hearing, during which Chen Yuqing described how he had been searched. Huang then identified himself as Huang Dongchen, currently a detective in the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and claimed that he was passing by the North Railway Station when he saw Chen and others arguing by the roadside, so he stepped in to mediate. The district chief, based on the evidence, immediately contacted the detective team. Team leader Lu, upon hearing the news, said that Huang was indeed a detective in the team, but he had not been ordered to inspect pedestrians in that area. He immediately ordered detective Zhou to go to the Fourth District Headquarters to clarify the situation. Zhou, accompanied by the police officer, first went to Huang's home and brought the detective license and gun to the district headquarters. Detective Zhou then took Huang, along with his gun and license, back to the team. Huang was first detained, and the incident was reported to Bureau Chief Chen. Bureau Chief Chen was furious, as Huang had neither received orders from his superiors nor carried his license or gun, yet he had arbitrarily gathered people to search pedestrians, which clearly indicated ulterior motives. He ordered Huang to be temporarily detained. As for the plaintiff, Chen Yu, he has been transferred to the Judicial Section by the Fourth District for further investigation.

Defalcation of Over a Million: Shen Chengfu Flees

Cotton Buyer of Tahe Foreign Firm

Court Issues Arrest Warrant, Search Proves Fruitless

Only Three of Shen's Cars Recovered

Police Discover He Fled to Qingdao

Shen Chengfu, a native of Shaoxing, age 36, was the junior owner of Zhihe Money Exchange. He resided at No. F2, Lane 1168, Jing'an Temple Road, Jing'an Temple. He was employed as a buyer in the cotton department of the British Tahe Foreign Firm at No. 15, Museum Road. Recently, he sold the firm's cotton, but did not remit the payments to the firm owner, embezzling them for his own use. The amount reached over a million, a matter discovered by the firm owner. Knowing he could not remain in Shanghai, Shen secretly fled with his entire family. The firm then reported the matter to the General Inspectorate of the Shanghai Municipal Police, who in turn requested the First Special District Court to issue an arrest warrant. The search proved fruitless. Zhang Zhiqing, the Chinese Detective Inspector of the General Inspectorate, and Geng Debiao, the detective, along with the Western Detective Inspector Huai Aituo, recovered three of Shen's cars. Yesterday morning, Ru Bao-yi, the police lawyer, requested the Special Court to dispose of them, stating the locations where they were found: (1) A Chrysler, No. 47, found at Aixueke Xuzi; (2) A Peugeot, No. 454, found at Aixueke Xuzi; (3) An Austin, No. 4702, found at Aixueke Xuzi. The first two cars were found at No. 38, Nanyang Road, and the third at the Mobil Automobile Repair Shop at No. 74, Beijing Road, discovered by the detectives. The police now know that Shen has fled to Qingdao, so they are requesting the court to reissue the warrant for general arrest, to facilitate sending personnel to Qingdao to apprehend him. Xu Jia-shi, the chief of the criminal court, reported the case, and it was ordered that, as Shen Chengfu's arrest has not been achieved, a general warrant should be reissued. The three cars are approved for detention and will be temporarily stored at the police station as collateral.

Municipal Council Opens Two Parks

The Zhu Chen family must treat their adopted daughter well.

Zhu Zhao-di, a nine-year-old girl from Haining, Zhejiang, was given to Zhu Chen, who runs a pancake shop at No. 85, Zhoushan Road, as an adopted daughter for a certain price due to her family's extreme poverty. Since entering the household, she has been repeatedly abused by her foster mother. Besides being assigned dangerous tasks, she is often beaten with firewood for minor offenses. Neighbors, feeling indignant, righteously reported this to the Chinese Children's Welfare Association. The association sent staff members, accompanied by Chinese and Western detectives from the Huishan Police Station, to investigate. After taking detailed statements, they brought Zhu Chen and Zhao-di to the police station for questioning. Zhu Chen confessed to the beatings. Finding no injuries on Zhao-di, they gave Zhu Chen a severe warning in person. Meanwhile, undercover detectives will continue to investigate, and the girl will be temporarily returned to the Zhu Chen family for a trial period to show leniency. If any further abuse is found, they will be arrested according to the law without fail. It is said that Zhu Chen, after receiving this warning, wants to improve her adopted daughter's life and does not want to abuse her again.

Violent Incident of Competition Between Male Patrons

Jin Ying-pei Beaten and Injured, Lin Ying Detained Awaiting Sentencing

Jin Ying-pei, an 18-year-old Guangdong native residing at No. 5, Xinchang Lane, Tiantong Road, worked as a water meter installer at the Anmei Foreign Firm on Dixiwei Road. At 2:25 PM on the 10th of this month, near the Xin'ailun Cinema on Haining Road, he was suddenly beaten to the ground by a fellow Guangdong native and stabbed in the back and abdomen with a knife, causing profuse bleeding. The Hongkou Police Station dispatched Chinese Detectives Liang Yong-ji and He Cheng-rui to the scene, who transported the injured person to Tongren Hospital for treatment and arrested a suspect, Lin Ying, a Guangdong tea boy, at the Hongkou Grand Hotel on North Sichuan Road. He was taken to the First Special District Court for interrogation and denied the charges. According to the police investigation, both the defendant and the injured person were patrons of Yue Jiulan, a Cantonese prostitute at No. 1142, North Jiangxi Road. The cause of the conflict was jealousy. However, the prostitute fled after the incident and is nowhere to be found. It was ordered that the case be re-examined after Jin recovers. Yesterday morning, the hearing resumed. Judge Shen Jiong-rong of the Third Criminal Court interrogated the parties. According to the police lawyer Li Zhi-shan, the prostitute Yue Jiulan was still impossible to apprehend. It was learned that the plaintiff was a member of the Xinli'an Club, and the defendant was a member of the Gonghele and Xin Shenhe Clubs. Fights often occur among the members of these clubs. The plaintiff Jin Ying-pei stated that he was going to see a movie at the Xin'ailun Cinema on Haining Road and had just arrived at the entrance when he saw a group of people fighting. He was trying to avoid them, but because he was wearing wooden clogs, he couldn't move quickly enough and was knocked down by someone in a white shirt and shorts, who stabbed him twice in the back and abdomen with a knife. He saw the defendant standing by watching, but he didn't make a move. He had played mahjong with him a few times but had no arguments. He hired lawyer Wu Shao-shan for defense. The defendant insisted that he was out shopping at the time and was just passing by watching, and he knew nothing about the incident. He had never met the plaintiff and had never played mahjong with him. He pleaded for justice and also hired a lawyer for defense. After examining the testimonies, Judge Shen ordered the defendant to be detained and set a date for sentencing.

The Case of the Watermelon Peel

Jiang A-san Dies from Injuries, Chang San-ren Flees

Jiang A-san, a thirty-six-year-old Ningbo native, resided at No. 6, Qingyun Lane, West Huade Road. At around 10:00 PM on the 21st of this month, he was eating watermelon in the lane. After eating, he threw the watermelon peel on the ground. At that time, a vagrant named Chang San-ren was also there, and the watermelon peel landed on his foot. A dispute arose. Chang slapped Jiang A-san and kicked him, causing injuries. His friend Shen Bao-cheng accompanied him to the Zhabei Red Cross Hospital for treatment. It was ineffective, and he died from his injuries at 10:00 AM on the 24th. The Hongkou Police Station was notified and ordered Detective Shen De-hui to investigate. The suspect had already fled. The body was transported to the Philander Road morgue for examination. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied forensic doctor Wei Li-gong and clerk Liu Chun to the morgue for examination. Witnesses Shen Chen, Shao Li, and others testified that they saw Chang San-ren beat Jiang A-san and then dispersed them. Guo Yu ordered that the deceased Jiang A-san died from injuries sustained during his lifetime, and Chang San-ren is suspected of committing a crime. The police will strictly apprehend the suspect for investigation. The body was handed over to Shen Bao-cheng, who signed a guarantee to collect and bury it.

However, in June and July, he privately embezzled 500 yuan of funds for personal use. Furthermore, on the 8th of this month, he absconded with 350 yuan in cash. The police lawyer Chen Ming stated the details of the case. Furthermore, Weng Zhao-tang, the general manager of the Disheng Pawnshop, complained about the defendant's embezzlement. Junkers Aircraft...Three

Rice Market in the Storm

Rice Price Limited to Seventeen Yuan, Sale of Polished Rice Prohibited

The Wuchen Society reports: The price of rice has been gradually declining to 17 yuan per shi due to the Social Affairs Bureau's multiple adjustments. However, some rice merchants are still insincere and undermine the efforts. A notice was specially issued yesterday and posted in the North and South rice markets to serve as a warning. Furthermore, in view of the fact that polished rice not only wastes resources but also hinders health, the rice shops and trade associations are instructed to no longer seek polished rice for the market. Yesterday, the price of rice suddenly rose by about one yuan per shi due to the severe weather. After the investigators reported to the bureau, the bureau immediately instructed the rice merchants that the storm was a temporary phenomenon and that they must not hoard with the intention of making a profit. Therefore, the price of rice has not risen sharply. The notice and instructions are excerpted as follows: Notice: This year's floods in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River have caused a disastrous autumn harvest, which is expected. The harvest in Gao Tian is still acceptable, and the early rice harvest in Zhejiang and southern Jiangsu is quite abundant. The late rice is also developing well. The rice fields in Pudong are better than ever before. Moreover, after last year's bumper harvest, the grain reserves in various places are not meager. There should be no concerns about maintaining the current food supply. However, some rice dealers and hoarders are taking advantage of the natural disasters to raise rice prices, disregarding the people's difficulties. They are violating orders and disregarding discipline, unaware of self-reflection. This bureau takes the welfare of the public as its welfare. Therefore, these harmful elements, although leniency has always been the policy, cannot be tolerated. This special notice is hereby issued to all rice merchants, peddlers, and hoarders. After this notice, the highest price of japonica rice in this city is 17 yuan per shi, and the middle and lower grades are priced accordingly. If there is any secret price fixing, hoarding, or intentional harm to the food supply of the citizens, once discovered, it will be severely investigated and dealt with, and no leniency will be shown. This is hereby notified. The instruction to rice merchants is as follows: In order to comply with the order, the prohibition of milling refined rice is to enrich the people's food and focus on hygiene. Previously, this bureau had submitted a request to the municipal government and then to the Executive Yuan for approval, and a general order was issued to all provinces and cities to comply with and publicize the case. However, it was found that the rice shops are still providing refined rice to the citizens. When there is incoming rice, they compete to purchase it, and even transport it from the place of origin to Shanghai for sale. This has created a trend for unscrupulous merchants to hoard goods and is often a medium for high rice prices. After the floods, the hidden worries of a disappointing autumn harvest are deepening. The disaster victims are waiting to be fed, and every grain is difficult to obtain. However, they are still wasting resources and ruining God's gifts. Although every grain is sought after, or it is out of the needs of the citizens, this industry can always think that the people's food is difficult to maintain, and the bad habits should be eliminated as soon as possible. The government orders should always be adhered to, and they should not be sold together. Even if citizens want to eat it, they cannot get it. This bureau deeply considers the regulation of people's food and should proceed from all parties to achieve it. There are also people who are wise and know the truth in this industry. Therefore, they should be kindly informed that they should no longer seek refined rice for sale, and even when citizens come to buy it, they should also be informed of the harm of eating it, which not only damages people's food but also harms hygiene. We should all think of the difficulties of resources and share the abundance of national food. In addition to the public notice, the association is hereby ordered to immediately forward the order to the industry to comply and print it out for all rice shops to post in obvious places, so that everyone knows it. Do not violate it.

Silk Industry Public Bonds Will Soon Begin to Be Claimed

The bonds have been printed and stored in the Central Bank of this port.

Manufacturers in Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Wuxi to Hold Regular Meetings

The Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds have already been issued by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry. The procedure for claiming them has also been properly negotiated. Once the Fund Management Committee receives them, the claiming process will begin. The silk factories associations of Zhejiang, Shanghai, and Wuxi will hold a general meeting on a regular basis. The details of the various situations are recorded below.

Seeking Instructions from the Minister: At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, Mu Ouchu of the Silk Industry Public Bond Executive Committee and Liu Manruo of the Fund Management Committee visited Industry Minister Kong Xiangxi for instructions. Minister Kong immediately telegraphed the ministry for inquiries. Yesterday, the Ministry of Industry replied, saying that the bonds had already been printed and stored in the Central Bank of Shanghai. The Public Bond Fund Management Committee will formally submit a request to receive them. Once received, they will begin to be issued to the manufacturers for claiming.

Claiming Procedure: The Silk Industry Public Bond Executive Committee, Chu Hui-seng, Shen Hua-chen, and Qian Feng-gao, have reached an agreement with the Fund Management Committee, Liu Man-ruo. According to the procedure, the Shanghai, Wuxi, and Zhejiang Silk Factory Associations will issue certificates, which the manufacturers will take to the Fund Management Committee to claim the bonds according to the number of machines they own. The manufacturers must also solemnly pledge that after receiving the bonds, they will strive to revitalize and rectify their operations in accordance with the instructions of the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Finance.

Association Meeting: Shen Hua-chen, the chairman of the Shanghai Silk Factory Association, has specially scheduled a general meeting of members for 4:00 PM today to report on the issuance of silk industry public bonds, the claiming procedures, and to discuss the Factory Law, the autumn silkworm market, and other matters. It is said that the Zhejiang and Wuxi Silk Factory Associations have also scheduled general meetings of members to report on the matter.

Silk Market and Silkworm Situation: There are 25 single-cocoon silk factories in Zhejiang, 48 single-cocoon silk factories in Wuxi, 106 single-cocoon silk factories in Shanghai, and 8 double-cocoon silk factories. Last month, 36 silk factories in this city were operating. Yesterday, the number has increased to 42. In the silk market, 20-22 thread count, 80% Evenness, for sales to the United States is priced at 920-930 taels per dan. 13-15 thread count, for sales to France, A is approximately 1,040 taels per dan, B is approximately 1,000 taels, and C is approximately 900 taels. It is expected that after the silk industry public bonds are issued, the number of operating silk factories may increase further.
